S. Dvivedi’s translation of the emended text :тАФCalculate the number of pakshas (parvans)85.”) elapsed since the beginning of the lustrum up to the required paksha of any of the twelve months (of the current year); multiply the number of pakshas by eleven. The product will be the Nakshatra-Am┼Ыas of the moon. In the case of a white paksha, add half of рднрд╛рдВрд╢$\left( {\frac{рез~реи~рек}{2}or~62} \right)$to the above product, the result will be the Nakshatra- Am┼Ыas of the moon.

For the proof of the above translations, see S. Dvivedi’s Bh─Бshya P. 24-25.

I now leave it to learned readers to judge for themselves which of the two is correct and more sensible, either B├бrhaspatya’s translation or S. Dvivedi’s emendation and translation.

рдп (резрем). In this verse it is not stated what thing is to be calculated; different ellipses therefore may be supplied by different expounders. B├бrhaspatya under a mistaken idea took рд╕рдкреНрддрдЧреБрдг to mean seven. (Vide his Jyotisha-Ved├бnga, P. 54-55.) He seems to think that this verse explains how to find out the hour-angle of any parvan. As Jyautisha-Ved├бnga treats of nothing

about hour-angles, and as the time occupied in traversing nakshatras is calculated according to рдп(резрем), I think his translation and explanation are both incorrect. S. Dvivedi’s emendation and translation tend to remove the obscurity of рдп (реиреж). I therefore hold that he is right. (See his Bh├бshya. p. 25-26.)

рдп (резрен). Here, the astrological parts of the Ved├бnga are correctly expounded by Som├бkara, though they are explained in different ways by B├бrhaspatya and S. Dvivedi. S. Drivedi’s explanation of (рдЬрд╛рд╡рд╛рджреНрдпрдВрд╢реИрдГ рд╕рдордВ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рддреН) is the best of all, as it shows the use of рдп (резрео). (Vide B├бrhaspatya’s Jyotisha-Ved├бnga p. 67 and S. Dvivedi’s Bh├бshya, p. 28-30).

рдп (резрео). This verse was correctly explained before by Som├бkara. (See Som├бkara Bh├бshya p. 30-32). The meaning of this verse was discovered by Dr. Thibaut also by tabulation, but the rule was left unsolved by him. B├бrhaspatya has solved it by aid of an indeterminate equation, for he was not aware of the ancient Hind├║ Kuttaka method. (Vide his Jyotisha-Ved├бnga, p. 51-52). Now S. Dvivedi has worked it out very easily by the ancient Hind├║ algebraic method. (Vide his Bh├бshya, p. 28-30.).

For рдо See my Vivarana, p. 76.

рдп (резреп). B├бrhaspatya’s translation of this verse fixes no rule and his long explanation produces no proper results. Jyautisha-Ved├бnga has no trial method; even then he says “It will be found on trial that the figures easiest to handle are those given in the text.” (Vide his Jyotisha- Ved├бnga, p. 57-58) In my opinion the trial method was not at all required here. I therefore recommend the reader to consider S. Dvivedi’s Bh├бshya, p. 33-34. I think his emendation can claim the same authority as that of B├бrhaspatya.

рдп (реиреж). Som├бkara’s explanation of this verse relates to y├бgn-k├бla, and so nothing is said about it. B├бrhaspatya’s translation and explanation are beyond the scope of the text. (Vide his Jyotisha-Ved├бnga, p. 58-59).

As regards his incorrect translation, the reader is referred to the examples given in my Vivarana, p. 77. In this verse the moon’s nakshatra is calculated on the given tithi as the sun’s nakshatra in рдп(реирел). Hence by calculating the tithi-nak-shatra by the ordinary method, taking the Jyautisha-Ved├бnga’s elements, it is clear that the emendation of S. Dvivedi is right and ingenious. I am sure that this emendation is based on the same authority as those of рдп(резрей), рдп (резреп) and рдп (рекреж).

For the meaning of (рдЕрд░реНрдХрджрд╢рд╛рднреНрдпрд╕реНрддрд╛рдореН), see my Vivarana, p. 77-78.

рдп (реирез). B├бrhaspatya’s translation that ’the sum of these K├бla’s represents the Kal├б’s corresponding to the entry of the moon into that tithi’s nakshatra’ is not correct. (See his Jyotisha-Ved├бnga, p. 58).

The tithi’s nakshatra and its am┼Ыas are calculated by рдп(реиреж) and the kal├бs corresponding to the entry of the moon into that tithi’s nakshatracan be easily calculated from the nakshatra- am┼Ыas by рдп (резреп).

B├бrhaspatya’s explanation of the verse is quite incorrect. See my vivarana, p. 78-79.

B├бrhaspatya in the appendix to his Jyotisha-Ved├бnga, p. vii also admits this. He writes. “My translation and explanation are defective, but those given by Mr. Dikshit are correct.” The translation should run thus, “Having multiplied the (elapsed) parvans by eleven and the (serial number of the current) tithi by nine, the double resalt (reduced to nakshatras), together with the (number of elapsed) parvans, gives the present nakshhatra of the sun, reckoned from the beginning of Sravistha. Bat I am unable to accept the following rendering of рдпреБрдЧрд▓рдмреНрдзрдореН as given by P. Sudh├бkara, “the result obtained by means of 124 the number of parvans contained in a yuga.”

The latter portion of this observation of B├бrhashpatya is quite mistaken. P. Sudh├бkara’s translation and explanation agree with those of Mr. Dikshit. Mr. Dikshit’s translation on mahrathi runs thus:

тАЬрдЧрдд рдкрд░реНрд╡рд╕рдВрдЦреНрдпреЗрд╡репреп рдиреАрдВ рдЧреБрдгреВрди рддреНрдпрд╛ рдЧреБрдгрдХрд╛рд░рд╛рдВрдд рддрд┐рд░реНрдереЛрд╕реп рдиреАрдВрдЧреБрдгреВрди рдЖрд▓реЗрд▓рд╛ рдЧреБрдгрд╛рдХрд╛рд░ рдорд┐рд▓рд╡рд╛рд╡рд╛, рдмреЗрдЬреЗрд╕ резреирек рдиреАрдВ рднрд╛рдЧ рд╡реЗрдВ, рднрд╛рдЧрд╛рдХрд╛рд░рд╛рдВрдд рдкрд░реНрд╡ рд╕рдВрдЦреНрдпрд╛ рдорд┐рд▓рд╡рд╛рд╡рд╛ рд╣реНрдордгрдЬреЗ] [рджреГрд╖реНрдЯ рддрд┐рдереНрдпрд╛рдВрддреАрдВ] рд╡рд░реНрддрдорд╛рди рд╕реВрд░реНрдп рдирдХреНрд╖рддреНрд░ рдирд┐рдШреЗрди. рд╣реИрдВ рдХрдорд╛рдиреЗрдВ рдЬрд╛рдгрд╛рд╡реЗрдВ. рдпреБрдЧрд╛рдВрдд рдкрд░реНрд╡реЗ резреирек рдЕрд╕рддрд╛рдд рд╣реНрдорд╛рдЧреЛрд╖реНрдареАрд╕ рдЕрдиреБрд╕рд░реВрди рдпреБрдЧ рд╢рдмреНрджрд╛рдЪрд╛ рдЕрд░реНрде рдпрд╛ рд╢реНрд▓реЛрдХрд╛рдВрдд резреирек рдЕрд╕рд╛ рдЖрд╣реЗ ……” (Vide His history of Indian Astronomy, p. 58.)

Multiply the number of the elapsed parvans by eleven and the (serial number of the current) tithi by nine, add them together.

This sum divided by 124, together with the number of the elapsed parvans, gives the present nakshatra of the sun.

The re-translation of this verse given by B├бrhaspatya in the appendix to his Jyotisha-Ved├бnga, p. vii is again vague and incorrect.

рдп (реирем). Owing to his defective knowledge of Hind├║ Astronomy B├бrhaspatya translates ‘рд╢реЗрд╖’ into ‘quotient’ and seems to think that this verse lays down a rule for the calculation of the sun’s motion (in the equinoctial circle) per lunar day. (Vide his Jyotisha-Ved├бnga, p. 45).

In Jyautisha-Ved├бnga, this motion of the sun is of no use. Not to speak of Jyautisha-Ved├бnga, such motion is nowhere mentioned in any treatise on modern Hind├║ Astronomy. I therefore think that S. Dvivedi’s explanation is right. His anvaya of this verse too is as clear as those of рдп (реирел), рдп (рейреп) etc., (See his Bh├бshya, p. 42-43). His emendations are evolved, as usual from the results obtained by arithmetical calculations.

рдп (реирен). Here it is not stated what calculation is to be made. In interpreting this verse, therefore, ellipses (рдЕрдзреНрдпрд╛рд╣рд╛рд░) supplied by different writers may vary according to the ways in which they set out to explain it.********************

******************** B├бrhaspatya thinks that the text, here, gives the approximate number of lunar days contained in the time of termination of the sun’s association with a nakshatra.********************

******************** If we reflect for a moment why the author of Jyautisha-Ved├бnga should take a wrong number when he knew the correct one and why he should here neglect the fraction, $\frac{1}{36}th$of a lunar day, which is much greater than 7 kal├бs in рдп(рейреп) where it was not neglected by him, then the whole translation and explanation of B├бrhaspatya fall to the ground and appear fanciful. No such lunar days are of any use in Jyautisha-Ved├бnga or modern Hind├║ Astronomy. S. Dvivedi’s translation and explanation of this verse, therefore, should be accepted without the least objection. (See his Bh├бshya, p. 44-45).********************

******************** рдЛ (резреп). Owing to his defective knowledge of Hind├║ Astronomy, B├бrhaspatya, in the first half of the verse, translates ‘рдЧреБрдгрд╛рднреНрдпрд╕реНрддрд╛рдиреН’ into the eighth group of stars’ and ‘рдкреНрд░рд╛рдЧреНрд╡рд┐рд▓рдЧреНрдирд╛рди’ into ’equatorial nakshatra,’ and in the second half of the verse ‘‘рд╖рдбрднреНрдпрд╕реНрддрд╛рдиреН"into multiplied by ‘six’. *рдЛ (рез), рдЛ (реи), рдЛ (рей), (2), (a). etc., denote the first, second, third etc., verse of the traditional text of the rik recension.********************

******************** If тАШkrittikas’ were meant by рдкреНрд░рд╛рдЧреНрд╡рд┐рд▓рдЧреНрдирд╛рдиреН рд╡рд┐рдирд┐рд░реНрджрд┐рд╢реЗрддреН’ then why did not the author of Jyautisha-Ved├бnga directly designate ‘krittikas’ the East star as he directly referred to ┼Ъravishth├б and A┼Ыlesha in рдп(рен), and why did he make a rule for such a simple Definition?********************

******************** Lagna, a well known thing to Hind├║s, which fixes heaven’s situation for the performance of religious duties, was unknown to B├бrhaspatya. Hence the incorrect translation given by him. The word ‘рдкреНрд░рд╛рдЧреНрд╡рд┐рд▓рдЧреНрдирд╛рдиреН’ suggests ‘рдЗрд╖реНрдЯрдХрд╛рд▓’ time reckoned from the rising of ┼Ъravishtha), as the necessary ellipsis (рдЖрдзреНрдпрд╛рд╣рд╛рд░) to be supplied here. It should be noted that in Jyautisha-Ved├бnga one nycthemeron (рд╕рд╛рд╡рдирджрд┐рди) is divided into 124 parts, each part being called an am┼Ыa and that a nakshatra is divided into 124 parts, each part being called ‘рднрд╛рдВрд╢’ (nakshatram┼Ыa). Now in one nycthemeron (рд╕рд╛рд╡рдирджрд┐рди) or in its 124 am┼Ыas, all the twenty-seven nakshatras or their 27x124 am┼Ыas will enter the horizon one after the other. Therefore in theрдЗрд╖реНрдЯрдХрд╛рд▓ = e,$= e,\frac{27 \times 124 \times e}{124}or~27~ \times ~e$nakshatra-am┼Ыas will enter the horizon. Thus рдЗрд╖реНрдЯрдХрд╛рд▓ multiplied by 27 gives the nakshatra-am┼Ыas between ┼Ъravishth├б and the current nakshatra. This product when divided by 124 will give the number of stars between them.********************

******************** рдЧрдг (рднрдЧрдг = рдирдХреНрд╖рддреНрд░ = рдЧрдг = 27) can be thus taken to denote twenty-seven. Therefore, I find that the emendation, рдЧрдг in place of рдЧреБрдг gives the true meaning of the first half of the verse, relying upon arithmetical calculations which are the best guide in elucidating such obscure passages.********************

******************** The latter half of the verse has been also incorrectly explained by both B├бrhaspatya and Dikshit. (Vide B├бrhaspatya’s Jyotisha-Ved├бnga, p. 36-38 and Dikshit’s history of Indian Astronomy, p. 81). They here forgot all about the 7th verse of Y├бjusha, from the principle underlying which, it can be inferred that one complete revolution of the moon contains her six seasons********************

moon is called рдЖрд░реНрдХреНрд╖рдорд╛рд╕ or рдирд╛рдХреНрд╖рддреНрд░рдорд╛рд╕, (See the 31st verse of Y├бjusha or the passage of Garga on the page 17 of this book). Hence multiplying the number of such months by six, we get the number of the moon’s seasons. From the above facts it will appear that S. Dvivedi’s emendation, рдЖрд░реНрдХреНрд╖рд╛рддреНin place of рд╕реВрд░реНрдпрд╛рдиреНgives the true meaning of the latter half of the verse. The moon’s seasons of the kind, explained by B├бrhaspatya in his Jyotisha-Ved├бnga, p. 37-38 are not to be found in any Sanskrit book. The explanations of B├бrhaspatya and Dikshit are quite fanciful and anything but correct.

******************** рдЛ (рейрей). This verse gives the same result as found by the rule given in рдп(реирей), рдЛ (рейрез). It has been correctly explained by Dikshit. (See his history of Indian Astronomy, p. 84).S. Dvivedi’s emendations are meant to keep the words of the verse in proper order and correct form.********************

******************** рдЛ (рейрек). This verse does not involve any astronomical calculation. It has been wrongly numbered as the 34th verse of the Rik recension. The first half of the verse is in an altogether different metre from the latter half, which shows that there must be something wanting here. (See S. Dvivedi’s Bh├бshya. p. 68.)********************

******************** From B├бrhaspatya’s explanation of рдкрд░реНрд╡ (parvan) in his Jyotisha-Ved├бnga, p. 39 it is obvious that the meanings of Vaidic words are unknown to him, though he considers himself a scholar in Vaidic Astronomy. It is this pride of his which actuated him to designate our learned professor, Mah├бmahop├бdhy├бya Pandit Sudh├бkara Dvivedi, “Professor of non-Vedic (and not vedic also)87.”) astronomy at Benares,” (See the first page of the preface to his Jyotisha-Ved├бnga.)********************

******************** The true meaning of рдкрд░реНрд╡in Vaidic sense is given by Som├бkara, ‘рджреЗрд╡рд╛ рдЕрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН рдкреНрд░реАрдгрдиреНрддреАрддрд┐ рд╡рдЪрдирд╛рддреН’(See the page 19 of this book). ********************

тАФтАФтАФтЩжтАФтАФтАФ

рдп (рей), рдп (резрео), рдп (реирек), рдп (реирем), рдп (реирен), рдп (рекреж) and рдЛ (рейрек) are in different metres from the other verses of Jyantisha-Ved├бnga. The verses. in different metres seem to have been afterwards added from other sources to Jyautisha-Ved├бnga, which was before in the pure рдЕрдиреБрд╖реНрдЯреБрдкреНmetre, to make the meanings of some of the original venes of Jyautisha-Ved├бnga clearer to the reader; for, рдп (рей) explains рдп (реи) in a better form; рдп (резрео) was introduced for the explanation of рдЬрд╛рд╡рд╛рджреНрдпрдВрд╢реИрдГin рдп (резрен);

рдп (реирек) was introduced for the explanation of рдп (рео) and рдп (рейрео);
рдп (реирем) is another form of рдп (реирел);
рдп (реирен) is another form of рдп (рейреп);
рдп (рекреж) is another form of рдп (рео);
and the first half of рдЛ (рейрек) in which the latter half is wanting is another form of рднрд╛рджрд╛рдирдВ рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдЪреНрдЪрдЪреБрд░реНрджрд╢реНрдпрд╛рдореН in рдп (резрен).

******************** B├бrhaspatyain the appendix to his Jyotisha-Ved├бnga has often criticized S. Dvivedi’s anvayas, but he had better think more seriously of the anvayas of рдп (резрео), рдп (резрем), рдп (реирео), рдп (реирем), рдп (рейреп).What anvaya can give the true meaning of рд╕рд╕рдкреНрддрдХрдореН or рд╕рд╕рдкреНрддреИрдХрдореН (one day plus seven kal├бs) of рдп (рейреп) until the whole thing be verified by Arithmetical calculations. Anvayas of the verses of such books as Jyautisha-Ved├бnga are acceptable only when their results agree with those actually found by exact calculations.********************

Conclusion:тАФ

рдп (рез-резреи),рдп (резрек),рдп(резрен-резрео),рдп (реирек),рдп(реирео),рдп(рейреж-рейрем), рдп(рейрео),рдп(рекреи-рекрей),were more or less correctly explained by Som├бkara.

********************рдп (резрей),рдп (реирей), рдп (реирел),were more or less correctly explained byDikshit.
рдп (резрео), and рдп (рейреп-рекреж)were more or less correctly explained byDr. Thibaut. ********************

******************** Closely scrutinizing the whole work, it will be found that B├бrhaspatya has done nothing original, except that he gave the proof of a rule, already discovered by Dr. Thibaut by tabulation, by the aid of an indeterminate equation.********************

******************** In рдп (резрез), рдп (резреи), рдп (резрек) and рдп (резрен) no astronomical calculations are required. They have been differently interpreted by B├бrhaspatya and other expounders of Jyautisha-Ved├бnga, but Som├бkara’s explanations of these verses and the terminology used in them of Jyautisha-Ved├бnga are most acceptable, for Som├бkara’s opinions on religious points are authoritative.********************

******************** S. Dvivedi has now proved all the rules contained in the ┼Ыlokas which involve astronomical calculations. All these notes form part of his lectures given to us on Jyautisha-Ved├бnga when B├бrhaspatya criticised his Bh├бsha, and I have now compiled them for the benefit of the learnedpublic, and I may also note here that the Maithila pupils of S. Dviveli were provoked to write their Chikits├б, when B├бrhaspatya criticised his Bh├бshya with very unworthy remarks; but all this was quite uncalled for. Learned readers, I hope, will now find that there is nothing now in Jyautisha-Ved├бngawhich is obscure or left unexplained except рдЛ (рейрек) in which something still seems to be wanting.********************

MURALIDHARA JHA.
